Source Code

This is a reconstruction of the AGC program Luminary 99 Rev 0. It was the second release of the Lunar Module flight software targeted for use in Apollo 11, after Luminary 97. A bug (which had been around since at least Apollo 10, Luminary 69) was discovered in Rev 0 shortly before the Apollo 11 flight, resulting in a last minute revision into Rev 1, which is what actually flew rather than the Rev 0 presented here. A hardcopy of Rev 0 is known to exist — it belonged to AGC developer Allan Klumpp for many years — but unfortunately the Virtual AGC Project has not had access to that hardcopy. Thus the code you see here had been reconstructed (we believe accurately) rather than transcribed. The first step of the reconstruction of the Rev 0 source code was the transcription of the Rev 1 source code from a hardcopy in the MIT Museum collection. The process of reverting the active portion of the source code (i.e., other than program comments) from Rev 1 to Rev 0 was very minor, consisting only of moving the position of the STARTSB1 label in FRESH START AND RESTART. Allan had previously given us the checksums of the memory banks of Rev 0, and we have verified the program presented here has checksums identical to all banks of Allan's listing of Rev 0. The notations on Allan's Rev 0 program listing read, in part:

	GAP:  ASSEMBLE REVISION 099 OF AGC PROGRAM LUMINARY BY NASA 2021112-051

A single program comment is known to differ between Rev 0 and Rev 1, but these are harder to reconstruct and verify than changes to the active portion of the code. Thus it is possible that there are additional differences between the program comments in Rev 0 and Rev 1 that are unknown to us, and therefore are not reflected in the code presented here. 

000002,000002:                                                                                                  #  Copyright:    Public domain.
000003,000003:                                                                                                  #  Filename:     MAIN.agc
000004,000004:                                                                                                  #  Purpose:      Part of the reconstructed source code for LMY99 Rev 0,
000005,000005:                                                                                                  #                otherwise known as Luminary Rev 99, the second release
000006,000006:                                                                                                  #                of the Apollo Guidance Computer (AGC) software for Apollo 11.
000007,000007:                                                                                                  #                It differs from LMY99 Rev 1 (the flown version) only in the
000008,000008:                                                                                                  #                placement of a single label. The corrections shown here have
000009,000009:                                                                                                  #                been verified to have the same bank checksums as AGC developer
000010,000010:                                                                                                  #                Allan Klumpp's copy of Luminary Rev 99, and so are believed
000011,000011:                                                                                                  #                to be accurate.
000012,000012:                                                                                                  #  Assembler:    yaYUL
000013,000013:                                                                                                  #  Contact:      Ron Burkey <info@sandroid.org>.
000014,000014:                                                                                                  #  Website:      www.ibiblio.org/apollo/index.html
000015,000015:                                                                                                  #  Mod history:  2009-05-05 RSB  Adapted from Luminary131/MAIN.agc.
000016,000016:                                                                                                  #                2016-11-03 RSB  Removed duplicate page #1.
000017,000017:                                                                                                  #                2017-01-28 RSB  Renamed STABLE_ORBIT.agc.
000018,000018:                                                                                                  #                2017-08-01 MAS  Updated for LMY99R0.
000019,000019: 
000020,000020:                                                                                                  #  The contents of the "LMY99R0" files, in general, are transcribed
000021,000021:                                                                                                  #  from a digital images created from a hardcopy of the program residing 
000022,000022:                                                                                                  #  at the MIT Museum.  Many thanks to Debbie Douglas of the Museum, and
000023,000023:                                                                                                  #  to Paul Fjeld (who made the images). They have been lightly modified
000024,000024:                                                                                                  #  to be equivalent to LMY99 Rev 0, otherwise known as Luminary
000025,000025:                                                                                                  #  Revision 99. The resulting bank checksums have been verified to match
000026,000026:                                                                                                  #  AGC developer Allan Klumpp's listing of Luminary Rev 99.
000027,000027: 
000028,000028:                                                                                                  #  Notations on Allan Klumpp's document read, in part:
000029,000029: 
000030,000030:                                                                                                  #        ASSEMBLE REVISION 099 OF AGC PROGRAM LUMINARY BY NASA 2021112-051
000031,000031:                                                                                                  #        ...
000032,000032:                                                                                                  #        THIS LGC PROGRAM IS INTENDED FOR USE IN THE LM DURING THE MANNED
000033,000033:                                                                                                  #        LUNAR LANDING MISSION OR ANY SUBSET THEREOF.
000034,000034:                                                                                                  #        ...
000035,000035: 
000036,000036:                                                                                                  #  The page images themselves, as reduced in size (and consequently in
000037,000037:                                                                                                  #  quality) to be suitable for online presentation, are available at 
000038,000038:                                                                                                  #  http://www.ibiblio.org/apollo.  If you want to see the (much) higher
000039,000039:                                                                                                  #  quality digital images that Paul actually made, contact info@sandroi.org
000040,000040:                                                                                                  #  directly.
000041,000041: 
000042,000042:                                                                                                  #  This file is a little different from the other LMY99R0 files I'm providing, 
000043,000043:                                                                                                  #  in that it doesn't represent anything that appears directly in the original source.  
000044,000044:                                                                                                  #  What I (RSB) have done for organizational purposes is to split the huge monolithic
000045,000045:                                                                                                  #  source code into smaller, more manageable chunks--i.e., into individual source 
000046,000046:                                                                                                  #  files.  Those files are rejoined within this file as "includes".  It just makes
000047,000047:                                                                                                  #  it a little easier to work with.  The code chunks correspond to natural divisions
000048,000048:                                                                                                  #  into sub-programs.  In fact, these divisions are more-or-less specified by
000049,000049:                                                                                                  #  the source code itself.  Refer to the "TABLE OF SUBROUTINE LOG SECTIONS" at the
000050,000050:                                                                                                  #  very beginning of the file ASSEMBLY_AND_OPERATION_INFORMATION.agc.
000051,000051: 
000052,000052:                                                                                                  #  It may be reasonably asked why tens of thousands of lines of source are joined by
000053,000053:                                                                                                  #  means of inclusion, rather than simply assembling the source files individually and
000054,000054:                                                                                                  #  then linking them to form the executable.  The answer is that the original 
000055,000055:                                                                                                  #  development team had no linker.  The builds were monolithic just like this.
000056,000056:                                                                                                  #  There was a big emphasis on reusability of the code in the original project, 
000057,000057:                                                                                                  #  apparently, but this reusability took the form of inserting your deck of 
000058,000058:                                                                                                  #  punch-cards at the appropriate position in somebody else's deck of punch-cards.
000059,000059:                                                                                                  #  (Actually, I believe a tape-library method was used to avoid having to continually
000060,000060:                                                                                                  #  reload the card decks, but that doesn't change the basic principle.)
000061,000061:                                                                                                  #  So, indeed, the method of file-inclusion is a very fair representation of the 
000062,000062:                                                                                                  #  methods used in the original development ... with the improvement, of course,
000063,000063:                                                                                                  #  that you no longer have to worry about dropping the card deck.  On the other hand, 
000064,000064:                                                                                                  #  I wasn't there at the time, so I may have no idea what I'm talking about.
000065,000065: 
000066,000066:                                                                                                  #  Finally, note that the original Apollo AGC assembler (called "YUL") is no longer 
000067,000067:                                                                                                  #  available (as far as I can tell).  In fact, it was replaced by another assembler
000068,000068:                                                                                                  #  ("GAP") even before Apollo 11, but GAP is no more available than is YUL.  The 
000069,000069:                                                                                                  #  replacement assembler yaYUL accepts a slightly different format for the source 
000070,000070:                                                                                                  #  code from what YUL or GAP accepted, so the source code has been targeted for 
000071,000071:                                                                                                  #  assembly with yaYUL.
000072,000072: 
000073,000073:                                                                                                  #  What follows is simply a bunch of file-includes for the individual code chunks.
000074,000074:                                                                                                  #  I've marked the page numbers to make proof-reading easier.  Besides, the digital
000075,000075:                                                                                                  #  images of the assembly listing contains a lot of interesting tables (cross-
000076,000076:                                                                                                  #  referenced to page numbers) created by GAP, but not duplicated by yaYUL, so it's
000077,000077:                                                                                                  #  still valuable even if the source-files listed below are at hand.
000078,000078:
